**Breakfast.** Eaten with Luna whenever Luna is in residence. Without Luna she eats lightly and standing — fruit, bread, the Inhuman equivalent of tea (a hot herbal infusion she carries with her between residences; cargo manifests on the Astarith log her requisitioning the dried leaf in quantity). In Avengers and FF settings she has been observed sharing this morning tea with whoever else rises early — Jarvis on multiple occasions, Sue Storm during the Hickman tenure, Medusa nearly every morning during co-residence. The tea is **the most consistent social ritual in her file**; she uses the cup as a prop for low-stakes intimate conversation. Anyone who wishes a frank word with Crystal should seek her between 06:30 and 07:30, with a cup in hand.

---

## 3. Mid-Morning to Mid-Day Block — Work, Such As She Performs It

Her work pattern depends entirely on her current institutional embedding. Pattern across all embeddings: **she is reliably present, reliably punctual, reliably executes assigned tasks, and reliably does not generate new initiatives unless the household is in crisis.**

**In Attilan / Inhuman court phases.** Mornings devoted to formal court attendance: Royal Family councils when Medusa convenes them, ceremonial duties (greeting envoys, presiding over minor petitions), and during the Soule *Inhuman* run, recruitment briefings on newly emerged NuHumans. She takes notes — actual physical notes, in an Inhuman script — and is observed re-reading them later. She is the only member of the Royal Family who consistently maintains a personal written record of council proceedings. This is not strategic; it is the conscientious habit of someone who has been told most of her life that her job is to remember what she was told.

**In Avengers / FF phases.** Training room work mid-morning. She drills her elemental control against environment simulators, typically alone, typically for sixty to ninety minutes. Surveillance of training-room logs across the Avengers Mansion, the Compound, and the Baxter Building shows a near-identical session structure: warmup with water manipulation (the easiest for her, the one she finds calming), progression through earth and air, fire last and briefest. She **dislikes fire work** — visible reluctance, shorter sessions — which is at least partly displacement from the Johnny Storm associations; she has been observed cutting fire drills short when Johnny is in the building.

**In Royals-era / Astarith phases.** This is the singular departure. She rises earlier (approx. 05:00 ship-time), takes the bridge alone for the first watch, runs navigation diagnostics, and reviews crew reports before anyone else is awake. The latency between the alarm and her appearance on the bridge in *Royals*-era logs is the shortest of any senior crew member's. This is the only documented period in her life in which the first hours of her day are structured around tasks she herself defined.

**Diplomatic field-work.** Across the Abnett/Lanning Inhumans run and the Hickman *Infinity* tie-ins she demonstrates a specific working pattern: she prefers **face-to-face negotiation in modest rooms**, declines grand settings when she can, and is observed conducting most of her real diplomatic work in side-conversations during state functions rather than at the formal table. She metabolizes ambient social information very rapidly and uses the formal proceedings as cover for the genuine exchanges happening at her elbow.

---

## 4. Midday — The Luna Window

When Luna is in residence, **midday is sacred and non-negotiable**. She breaks from whatever she is doing — including, observably, mid-council and mid-mission — to be present for Luna's midday meal and the hour after. This is the most rigidly defended block in her schedule across every era. Handlers and household members who have attempted to schedule over it have learned, sometimes more than once, that Crystal will simply not be there.

When Luna is in Pietro's custody or otherwise absent, the midday hour is observably difficult for her. She fills it in patterned ways: a long walk through whichever environment she inhabits (the Attilan gardens, Central Park during Manhattan residency, the Astarith's botanical bay), often alone, often touching plants as she passes them — a small repeated gesture of contact-with-living-thing that reads as self-soothing. She has been recorded making this circuit at the same approximate time, in the same approximate route, for years at a stretch.

She **does not eat a structured lunch** when alone. She grazes — fruit, bread, tea — at her desk or on her walk.

---

## 5. Afternoon Block — The Most Variable

This is the working public-life block: missions, council, diplomatic calls, NuHuman recruitment trips (Soule era), Astarith command duties (Ewing era), child-rearing administration (custody coordination, school logistics, Terrigenesis-related medical appointments during Luna's adolescence).

Three behavioral constants survive across the variation:

**1. She takes a second tea between 15:00 and 16:00 local.** Unfailingly. In every residence, in every era. If interrupted at this hour she will accept the interruption gracefully but will be observed returning to the kettle within twenty minutes.

**2. She checks in on Luna.** Even when Luna is grown, even when Luna is on another world, even when Luna is in Pietro's custody, there is a documented afternoon contact attempt — a call, a message, a passing inquiry to whoever may have seen her. This has the rhythm of a compulsion, not a courtesy.

**3. She gravitates to a window.** In every residence the surveillance file documents her returning, repeatedly, to a specific window — usually the one with the most sky visible. She stands at it for two to ten minutes at a time, often more than once an afternoon. The behavior intensifies under stress. Likely substrate: the elemental aspect of her power-set is, by her own account in Englehart-era Avengers narration, *eased* by atmospheric contact; the window-gravitation reads as a low-grade homeostatic regulation, like a person opening a vent.

---

## 6. Evening Block (approx. 18:00–22:00)

**The evening meal is the social anchor.** Crystal will, given a choice, eat with people — family, household, crew. She does not enjoy eating alone and avoids it when possible. The meals are structured: in Attilan, formal court dining when court is in session, family-table dining when not; in Earth residences, whatever the household pattern is, taken on time. She is the household member most likely to wait for stragglers, most likely to set an extra place for an unexpected guest, most likely to ask the cook about the food. In *Royals* logs she eats with the crew rather than in private quarters — the only senior officer who routinely does.

After the meal: **Luna time** if Luna is present (story, conversation, supervised practice with Luna's own emerging abilities during the NuHuman phase). **Reading** if not — she reads, in Inhuman script, primarily history and natural-philosophy texts from the Attilan archive; she has been observed re-reading the same few volumes over years, a pattern more consistent with comfort-reading than scholarship. In Manhattan residences she has been observed reading human periodicals (fashion, gardening, occasionally political news), generally lightly.

**Bath, again, in the long evenings she is not on duty.** A second bath is a leisure indulgence, not a hygiene routine. She has been observed remaining in the water for more than an hour at a time during low-stress periods.

**Bedtime ritual.** A second breath-cycle. A check on Luna if Luna is present, performed by walking to her room and standing in the doorway for a count of breaths — she rarely enters. Lights low rather than off — she dislikes pitch darkness and uses ambient illumination, an unusual preference for an adult of her resources and explicable as a residue of the Maximus-siege childhood that drove her to the Fantastic Four in the first place.

---

## 7. Habits of Place

**Residence rotation.** Across her life she has held primary residence in: the Royal Quarter of Attilan (multiple physical incarnations of the city); the Baxter Building; Avengers Mansion and the West Coast Compound; her own Inhuman embassy suites in Manhattan; the royal residence on Hala during the Ronan marriage; New Attilan in the East River; the Astarith. The pattern is *serial monogamy of place* mirroring the serial monogamy of relationship. She does not maintain two residences; she lives wholly in the current one and abandons the prior almost completely.

**Within any residence she colonizes one specific room.** Not the bedroom — a sitting room or salon, where she keeps her tea, her current books, the personal correspondence she actually answers (she is a consistent letter-writer to a small circle: Medusa, Luna, a small number of long-standing friends). This room is invariably arranged with **plants and a water feature** when she has the latitude to arrange it. The water-feature preference is unmistakable across decades — fountains in Attilan, a fish tank in one Manhattan suite, an open viewing-port over a hydroponic bay on the Astarith. She does not name the preference; it is simply where she sits.

**Outdoor circuit.** In every residence she develops within days of arrival a **walking circuit** — a route she takes once or twice daily, the same way each time, at roughly the same hours. The route in Central Park during the Hickman era was a southeast loop from the FF residence; the route on New Attilan was the perimeter walk along the upper terrace; on the Astarith it is bow-to-stern along the spinal corridor. Surveillance heuristic: she is **predictable to within minutes** on these circuits, and on the rare occasions she breaks them, something is wrong.

---

## 8. Habits of the Body

- **Hand to hair when listening.** A repeated gesture, single fingertip drawn along the hairline at the temple. Increases in frequency when she is being asked something she does not want to be asked.
- **Slight backward weight-shift when disagreed with.** She does not step back, but the center of gravity moves. Trained negotiators across the Kree and Skrull files would have noted this.
- **Touches plants in passing.** Already noted; ubiquitous.
- **Heats her own drinks.** Reflexive use of low-grade thermal control rather than waiting for tea to steep at ambient temperature. She is unaware she does it in front of humans, who find it disconcerting.
- **Plays absently with water.** In any setting with a basin, fountain, or glass, she produces small idle manipulations — a ripple, a spiral — while thinking. The complexity of the manipulation tracks the depth of the thought.
- **Does not fidget verbally.** Unusually quiet conversational baseline; she does not use filler words, does not over-explain, lets silences sit. The court training is visible here.
- **Holds eye contact in conversation past human comfort norms.** This is read by humans as warmth or intensity depending on context; it is in fact Inhuman aristocratic standard and she does not modulate it for setting.
- **A specific small smile** at the corner of the mouth when she is being polite about something she dislikes. Universally legible to those who know her; she has never learned that it gives her away.

---

## 9. Habits of Time

She is **early**, consistently, for everything she has agreed to attend. She is **late**, consistently, for things she did not agree to but is expected to attend by family obligation — a passive-aggressive tell she would deny.

She marks anniversaries privately and conspicuously: the date of Luna's birth (observed quietly each year regardless of residence); the date of her own Terrigenesis (a small ritual involving a candle and a bowl of water, conducted alone, drawn from Inhuman tradition); the dates of certain losses (Ronan's death, the destructions of Attilan) — observed not with ceremony but with a withdrawn day, walks longer than usual, less spoken at meals.

She does not mark wedding anniversaries from any of her marriages.

---

## 10. The Reconstructed Week — What Surveillance Would Log

A representative week, mid-career, embedded in the Royal Family household on New Attilan, Luna in residence:

- **Day 1 (Council day).** Up 05:40. Bath, hair, green court attire. Tea with Medusa at 06:40, fifteen minutes, low conversation. Breakfast with Luna 07:30. Council from 09:00 to approx. 12:30; she takes notes, speaks twice, defers to Medusa on the substantive vote. Lunch with Luna and one of Luna's tutors 13:00. Afternoon: correspondence, a short walk on the upper terrace at 15:30 with her second tea taken at the end. Window-stand at the eastern observation gallery, eight minutes, twice. Evening meal with the Royal Family at 19:00. Reading with Luna 20:30. Bed 22:00.
- **Day 2 (Field day).** Up 05:30. Briefing in fatigues. Departs for a NuHuman recruitment site by morning. Operates competently in the field — first contact, calming presence, household assessment. Returns by late afternoon. Tea taken in transit. Evening normal. Bath longer than usual; one episode of mild atmospheric disturbance in her chamber that resolves within the hour. Bed 21:30, early.
- **Day 3 (Diplomatic).** Embassy work in Manhattan; she travels in and out the same day, avoiding overnight off-Refuge. Side-conversations more than formal table. Returns visibly tired. Skips evening reading; sits in her salon with Luna and a book for two hours, not reading, watching the water feature. Bed 22:15.
- **Day 4 (Quiet).** No external commitments. Long walk, both circuits. Two baths. Writes letters (Medusa absent for the day on Royal business). Reads. The day a handler would learn the most about her, because it is the day she is most herself — and the least eventful.
- **Day 5 (Luna's day).** Schedule entirely subordinated to Luna's activities. Attends whatever Luna attends. Observed adjusting her own posture to be slightly behind Luna's in shared settings — deferential motherhood, deliberate.
- **Day 6 (Crisis interruption).** A summons from Medusa or a security alert reshapes the day; she complies immediately, drops the walk, drops the tea schedule, executes. Returns to ritual the moment the crisis releases her. The speed with which the rituals re-form post-disruption is itself the diagnostic point: **the rituals are the regulation**, not preference.
- **Day 7 (Withdrawn).** Following the disruption, lower verbal output, longer window-times, an extra bath, the candle-and-bowl ritual conducted privately in the evening. By morning of the next cycle she is restored.

---

## 11. Operational Notes for the File

- **Best window for unscheduled approach:** 06:30–07:30, with tea, on her own ground.
- **Worst window:** the Luna midday hour; she will refuse, and will remember the attempt.
- **Most legible affect channel:** the local atmosphere of whatever room she is in. Watch the water surfaces. Watch the candle flames. Watch her hair.
- **Most reliable predictor of internal state:** the *complexity* of her idle water-manipulation. Simple ripple = at ease. Sustained spiral = thinking through something. Geometric forms = distressed and suppressing.
- **The single most stable element of her life:** the afternoon Luna-check. If it stops, something is catastrophically wrong.
- **The single most stable element of her self:** the tea ritual. It travels with her; it has outlived three marriages and two destroyed cities; it will outlive most of the people in her current file.

She lives, in summary, a life of **small invariant rituals layered over a wholly variable institutional scaffolding**. The rituals are how she remains *herself* through serial relocations, serial attachments, and serial reinventions imposed by others. A surveillance team that learns the rituals learns her — and learns, more importantly, the precise hours at which the latent agent under the dependent presentation is closest to the surface: alone, early, with tea, at a window, watching the weather she is partly responsible for.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*The family system that built her, in the order it shaped her.*

A general note before the individual dossiers: House Amaquelin is a cadet branch of Attilan's Boltagon-led royal line, and Crystal's entire childhood was conducted inside the Great Refuge's hothouse aristocracy — a closed gene pool of perhaps a few thousand souls, ordered by Terrigenetic caste, governed by a silent monarch, threatened recurrently by the deposed Maximus faction. The relevant fact is that she has never had what an Earth-human would recognize as an unmediated relationship. Every familial bond in her life was simultaneously a political relationship within the Inhuman court. She learned, before she learned to speak in full sentences, that "sister" and "queen" were the same word; that "uncle" and "usurper" could be; that the household and the state were not separable. This is the soil all of the following grew in.

---

## 1. QUELIN AMAQUELIN — Father (deceased)

The senior Amaquelin, head of the cadet noble house, died when Crystal was a child — canonically killed in the Trikon incident along with Medusa's and Crystal's mother Ambur, the catastrophe that orphaned both sisters and consolidated Medusa as Crystal's de facto parent. The file on Quelin is necessarily thin in terms of direct interaction data, because the relationship existed primarily as a *founding absence*.

**History.** Quelin and Ambur were members of the council surrounding King Agon and Queen Rynda; the Trikon — a runaway Terrigen-energy phenomenon — killed multiple senior Inhumans simultaneously. Crystal was, by every reasonable inference from the canonical timeline, between roughly six and ten years old at the loss. Medusa, several years older and already Terrigenized, became her guardian.

**Dynamics in absence.** What Crystal carries from Quelin is not memory of a man — her textual references to him are vanishingly rare across sixty years of appearances — but the structural fact of his absence: a paternal slot vacated early, never refilled by a single figure, instead distributed across Black Bolt's silent authority, Karnak's instructional severity, and (most consequentially) the surrogate-paternal weight she would later place on every senior male partner she took. Pietro received a great deal of that displaced paternal projection. Ronan received more. Even Johnny, in the early FF days when Reed was the household pater, was absorbed into a system in which the boyfriend-figure occupied a quasi-paternal seat she had no living father to anchor elsewhere.

**Trust/safety.** N/A — relationship terminated before adult bond was possible.

**Failure mode.** The original wound. A child not yet old enough to have internalized a stable paternal imago lost the man before the imago consolidated. What forms in that gap is not a clean grief but a chronic *receptivity* — an aperture in her psyche that any sufficiently attentive older male can address himself to. Every analyst handling her file should mark this as the deepest substrate of her romantic pattern.

**Leverage.** None directly. Indirect: invocations of her parents' memory, of "what your father would have wanted for Attilan," carry disproportionate weight in negotiations, particularly from Karnak or Medusa, who were old enough to know him as an adult.

---

## 2. AMBUR AMAQUELIN — Mother (deceased)

Killed in the same Trikon event. Even thinner direct record than Quelin.

**Dynamics in absence.** Crystal's relationship to her dead mother is mediated almost entirely through Medusa. What she knows of Ambur — her affect, her judgments, her standards of comportment, the way she wore the Amaquelin coiffure — she knows because Medusa told her, or because Medusa unconsciously embodied her. The result is an unusual fusion: Crystal's maternal imago and her sister are, at a level deeper than she can articulate, the same person.

**Trust/safety.** Imagined as total. The dead mother is the only attachment figure who never disappointed her, because she had no chance to.

**Failure mode.** The idealization of the lost mother sets an unmeetable standard. Medusa, who is the closest living approximation, can never be fully sufficient — and this constant small insufficiency is part of why Crystal both reveres and quietly chafes against her sister.

**Leverage.** Operative through Medusa, not directly accessible.

---

## 3. MEDUSALITH BOLTAGON, née AMAQUELIN — Sister, Queen, surrogate mother

The single most determinative relationship of Crystal's life. Everything else in her file is downstream of this one.

**History.** Medusa is the elder by perhaps six to eight years — old enough that when the Trikon orphaned them, she was already a young woman, already Terrigenized, already betrothed within the royal program to Black Bolt. She raised Crystal. The phrase is precise: Medusa, not nursemaids and not the Genetics Council, raised her. She brushed the child's hair, taught her court protocol, sat by her bedside through her own Terrigen cocooning, presented her to the throne when the gift manifested. Every formative authority Crystal recognizes was first Medusa's voice.

**Dynamics — early.** Adoring. The Lee/Kirby material shows Crystal as visibly the baby — bright, eager, slightly indulged, granted small disobediences. Medusa's tenor toward her is consistently protective with an edge of fond exasperation. When Crystal runs off to live with the Fantastic Four, Medusa does not stop her, but the textual undercurrent is unmistakable that the elder sister considers this a phase to be tolerated. The expectation of return is built into the permission to leave.

**Dynamics — middle decades.** The marriage to Pietro and the birth of Luna shifted the balance only superficially. Medusa remained the figure to whom Crystal reported, the queen whose silent assessment she sought, the sister whose disappointment was the worst possible weather. The Norm Webster affair is instructive here: Crystal hid it from Pietro, of course, but she hid it from Medusa *harder*. The asymmetry of concealment maps the asymmetry of judgment-power.

**Dynamics — recent.** The Soule *Inhuman* run is the clearest data on the mature pattern. Medusa, now reigning queen-regnant during Black Bolt's absences, deploys Crystal as her field commander, her recruiter of NuHumans, her envoy. Crystal accepts. The competence she demonstrates in this role is real and substantial. But the directional flow remains absolute: Medusa decides, Crystal executes. Even in *Royals*, when Crystal pilots the Astarith on a quest of cosmic stakes, the mission is framed as Medusa's tasking; the autonomy Crystal exercises is autonomy within an assignment.

**Trust/safety.** Functionally absolute on Crystal's side. She would entrust Luna to Medusa without hesitation; would die on Medusa's order; would believe Medusa's account of a contested fact over her own perception. From Medusa's side: trust is real but bounded by the queen's prior loyalty to the crown and the species. Medusa would sacrifice Crystal if Attilan required it. Crystal knows this and accepts it as the correct moral order. This is the *system* both sisters operate inside, and neither questions it.

**Evolution.** The bond has shifted from mother-daughter (childhood) to queen-and-favored-courtier (court years) to commander-and-lieutenant (Soule/Ewing) — with the underlying emotional content invariant. The clothes change; the dependency does not.

**Failure mode.** Crystal cannot disagree with Medusa effectively. She can sulk, she can drag her feet, she can comply slowly — passive-aggressive resistance is the maximum expression of disagreement available to her in this register. Direct confrontation is missing from her repertoire. This is the central engine of her dependent-traits presentation: the template was set with Medusa and now generalizes to every authority figure she internalizes as familial.

**Leverage.** Highest of all human leverage on the subject. Any communication delivered in Medusa's name, or any operation framed as serving Medusa's interest, will receive substantially more compliance than the same operation framed neutrally. Conversely, *Medusa's expressed disapproval is the single most effective sanction available against her*. The handler who controls Medusa's voice controls Crystal at the deepest accessible level.

**Subsidiary fact.** Medusa's hair — sentient, prehensile, longer than her body — is the single most familiar physical object in Crystal's life. The image of those tendrils carrying her as a child, restraining her in adolescent tantrums, smoothing her own elemental hair before court appearances, recurs in flashback panels across multiple runs. There is a tactile-memory layer here that is genuinely pre-verbal.

---

## 4. BLACK BOLT (BLACKAGAR BOLTAGON) — Brother-in-law, King

Crystal's relationship with Black Bolt is the relationship of a younger sister to her elder sister's silent, terrifying, beloved husband — and to her absolute monarch. The two roles are not separated in her mind; they cannot be.

**History.** Black Bolt was already the Genetics Council's chosen consort for Medusa when Crystal was a child. He entered her life as a figure already in his post-Terrigen voicelessness, already raised in the soundproofed Tower in which the royal family had quarantined him from infancy. To young Crystal he would have been an enormous, gentle, mute presence at the periphery of every meal and every state function — a man who could destroy the city with a syllable and so spoke none.

**Dynamics.** Affectionate distance. Black Bolt cannot speak to her; he can only sign, gesture, or have Medusa interpret. The bond is therefore mediated through Medusa structurally, which has the secondary effect of routing yet more of Crystal's emotional traffic through her sister. Black Bolt has, in canonical moments, expressed real fondness for Crystal — interceded for her in council, granted her latitude regarding her marriages, treated Luna with great tenderness. He does not micromanage her.

**Trust/safety.** She trusts him absolutely as a moral agent and as a king; she has never in canon questioned a Bolt decree on its own terms. The *safety* is more complex: any room containing Black Bolt is also a room one breath away from extinction, and Crystal grew up in this awareness. The unconscious vigilance is permanent. She has, since girlhood, monitored the king's affect with a low-grade continuous attention — not from fear of him *toward her*, but from a courtier's reflex of reading the weather of the throne.

**Evolution.** Largely static. The relationship has held the same shape across sixty years: respectful, warm-distant, mediated. *Infinity*, in which Black Bolt detonates Attilan as a strategic act against Thanos, was a profound shock to her, but she absorbed it as a king's necessary decision. She did not personalize it. This is significant — the same incident, processed by Maximus, generated decades of fratricidal grievance; processed by Crystal, generated grief and acceptance.

**Failure mode.** She will not press him directly. If she has a request, it goes through Medusa. If she has a grievance, it dies unspoken. This is the courtier's failure mode generalized to family.

**Leverage.** A direct command from Black Bolt — even a signed one — carries the force of religious obligation. Rare, therefore high-value. Should not be expended frivolously by any party seeking sustained access.

---

## 5. MAXIMUS THE MAD (MAXIMUS BOLTAGON) — Brother-in-law, recurrent usurper

The shadow uncle. The other Boltagon brother. The dangerous one.

**History.** Maximus is Black Bolt's younger brother — brilliant, unstable, repeatedly the architect of coups against his elder. Crystal first encounters him as the usurper from whom she is fleeing in *FF* #45; her introduction to Johnny Storm is, narratively, the consequence of her flight from Maximus's siege. He has, across the decades, made tactical use of her — sometimes as bargaining chip, sometimes as object of inappropriate possessive interest (notably in early-era material, in which Maximus's regard for his brother's sister-in-law had unmistakable predatory tones), occasionally as a sincere if manipulative ally during the brief windows in which he was nominally rehabilitated.

**Dynamics.** Wariness, well-founded, calibrated by long exposure. She is one of the few people who can be in a room with Maximus and remain neither charmed nor enraged — she has known him too long for either. She reads his cycles. She knows when he is in a remitted phase and when he is building toward something. This is genuine clinical-grade knowledge, accumulated over a lifetime of monitoring the family's most dangerous member.

**Trust/safety.** Low and conditional. She will accept his tactical contributions when sanctioned by Black Bolt or Medusa; she will not be alone with him by choice; she will not place Luna within his orbit unsupervised. These are settled defaults, not active calculations.

**Evolution.** From childhood fear (the usurper of her introductory storyline) to adult wariness to a kind of weary, almost fond, *recognition* — the late material (Hickman, Soule, Ewing) shows her able to banter with him, even occasionally enjoy his rhetorical pyrotechnics, while maintaining the underlying perimeter. She has matured in this relationship more visibly than in many others, possibly because it never had the dependency component her other family bonds carried — Maximus was never safe enough to depend on, so she developed actual judgment with him.

**Failure mode.** She will sometimes underestimate the speed of his decompensation. Having watched him cycle many times, she trusts the cycle — and is occasionally caught when he breaks the rhythm.

**Leverage.** Maximus knows things about her — childhood material, early infatuations, family secrets — that no one else living holds. He has used some of this and could use more. The risk vector here is informational rather than physical.

---

## 6. KARNAK MANDER-AZUR — Cousin

The philosopher-warrior of the royal cousinship; uncle-coded in family function despite the technical relation.

**Dynamics.** Karnak is the family's instructor — the one who sees the flaw in all things, including the flaw in Crystal's character. She knows he knows. He has, in canonical exchanges (especially the Warren Ellis *Karnak* miniseries and earlier *Inhumans* material), looked at her with the particular gaze that strips a person of their poses. She finds this both threatening and clarifying. He has never married her off, never positioned her romantically, never asked anything of her except, occasionally, to think more clearly than she would prefer to.

**Trust/safety.** She trusts his analysis and his loyalty to the family; she does not seek his company casually. He is not a comfort figure.

**Failure mode / leverage.** He is one of the few people who can name her patterns to her face. A directed observation from Karnak about her romantic decision-making would penetrate where no other family member's could. He has, mercifully, refrained from doing this often.

---

## 7. GORGON PETRAGON — Cousin

The cousin-as-elder-brother. Hooves, stamp-shockwaves, blunt loyalty.

**Dynamics.** Gorgon is the family's enforcer and Crystal's de facto male protector across decades of court politics. He is gentler with her than with anyone else — there are repeated panels across runs in which Gorgon's terrible aspect softens conspicuously in her presence. The bond is fraternal, uncomplicated, and one of the most genuinely *easy* relationships in her file.

**Trust/safety.** High. She would put her physical safety in his hands without hesitation and historically has. He has nearly died for her on multiple occasions.

**Failure mode.** Gorgon's loyalty is unconditional, which means he cannot check her bad decisions; he will defend the decision regardless. He is not a counter-weight.

**Leverage.** Threats to Gorgon's wellbeing move her substantially. His genuine displeasure with one of her choices would also register, more than Karnak's coldly correct disapproval would.

---

## 8. TRITON — Cousin

The aquatic cousin; the most reclusive of the royal kin.

**Dynamics.** Affectionate but the most distant of the cousin set, by virtue of his amphibious physiology and his preference for marine isolation. She is fond of him in a settled, low-frequency way — birthdays remembered, certain childhood games recalled, occasional cooperation on aquatic operations where her water control and his physiology pair naturally.

**Trust/safety.** High; bandwidth low.

**Leverage.** Limited operational salience.

---

## 9. CRYSTALS (LOCKJAW) — Family animal, teleporting bulldog

Not human, deserves a section nonetheless. Lockjaw has been a continuous presence in her life since girlhood — the family's giant teleporting canine, simultaneously a pet, a transport asset, a guardian, and in some interpretations a transformed Inhuman in his own right.

**Dynamics.** Crystal is one of Lockjaw's two or three favored humans (along with Medusa and, latterly, Kamala Khan in *Ms. Marvel*-adjacent material). He has carried her between worlds, slept across her feet through childhood illnesses, guarded Luna's cradle. The bond is wordless and total.

**Trust/safety.** Absolute, in both directions. Lockjaw is, after Luna and Medusa, the being Crystal most trusts in the universe.

**Failure mode.** None operationally relevant. Crystal's reliance on Lockjaw for emergency egress has, on occasion, atrophied her own planning for contingencies — the dog has always been there to teleport her out.

**Leverage.** Threats to Lockjaw produce a category of response in her closer to the Luna-axis than to ordinary affection. He is family in the strict sense, and operationally protected.

---

## 10. LUNA MAXIMOFF — Daughter

The center of gravity. The relationship that, in the dependency-mapping, *inverts* her pattern: with Luna, Crystal is the senior figure, the protector, the one who must decide. It is the only sustained relationship in her life in which she is structurally not the dependent party.

**History.** Conceived during the Pietro marriage, born under physiologically difficult circumstances (*Avengers* #200-era), initially non-powered — a fact that distressed Crystal disproportionately, because in Inhuman aristocratic culture an un-Terrigenized child is a child without a place. Luna was eventually exposed to Terrigen in later material (Lanning/Abnett era) and gained empathic-aura perception abilities. She has been a custody object in the Crystal-Pietro divorce wars, a target of Maximus and various enemies of the throne, a survivor of the Terrigen Cloud crisis, and, increasingly in recent runs, a young adult with her own positions.

**Dynamics.** Fierce, attentive, occasionally overcorrecting. Crystal's mothering style is warm and present but marked by anxious overprotection — entirely intelligible given that Luna has been kidnapped, endangered, and exposed to cosmic-level threats more times than most children survive even once. There are also documented periods (the late Pietro arc, the Ronan-Hala relocation) when Crystal placed Luna in Medusa's care for extended stretches because the operational situation was too dangerous. These separations weigh on her. Luna, for her part, has at various canonical moments expressed exasperation with both parents and chosen, in some arcs, to live with Pietro or with the larger royal household rather than with Crystal directly. This wounds her mother substantially but does not break the bond.

**Trust/safety.** Total from Crystal toward Luna in protective intent. From Luna toward Crystal: complicated by the divorce-era custody chaos and by the broader fact of growing up royal and endangered, but fundamentally intact.

**Evolution.** From infant (object of pure protection) to child (object of custody warfare) to adolescent (figure of independent judgment, source of mild grievance about parental inconstancy) to young adult (peer-coded in some recent material). Crystal has had to learn, against her instincts, to release Luna toward her own agency. She is not finished learning this.

**Failure mode.** Overprotection occasionally escalates to operational overreach — Crystal will breach protocol, defy command, ignore tactical necessity if Luna is on the line. This is the *only* axis on which she will defy Medusa, and she will do so absolutely.

**Leverage.** The highest-grade leverage available against the subject, of any kind, from any source. Any operation involving Luna's safety, real or perceived, will produce overriding behavioral response. Conversely, demonstrating reliable benevolent attention to Luna's welfare is the single most effective method of building durable trust with the subject. This is the file's most operationally significant single fact.

---

## 11. AHURA BOLTAGON — Nephew

Black Bolt and Medusa's son; Crystal's nephew; a troubled, dangerous, beloved boy.

**Dynamics.** Crystal is aunt-as-secondary-mother — a role she takes seriously, complicated by Ahura's own instability (the boy inherited some of Maximus's neurological vulnerabilities along with his father's destructive potential). She has cared for him in extended stretches when Black Bolt and Medusa were absent or warring. The *Royals* arc, in which Ahura is part of the cosmic expedition, deepens this — she is, for the duration of the quest, the closest adult relative present, and the maternal-aunt register is sustained and visible.

**Trust/safety.** She trusts him as family; she watches him as a known risk. The dual register is automatic, courtier-bred.

**Failure mode.** She will protect him past the point of strategic sense, on the Luna axis (extended). She will also, occasionally, fail to read his decompensation in time, because she does not want to.

**Leverage.** Substantial. Lower than Luna, higher than most cousins.

---

## 12. PIETRO MAXIMOFF — Ex-husband (covered in detail in Relationships II, noted here for family-structural completeness)

Listed here only to acknowledge that Pietro, by virtue of having been the father of Luna and a member of the extended royal-marital network, occupies a quasi-family slot in Crystal's psyche that has never fully closed despite the divorce. The romantic file is handled elsewhere; the *familial* residue is that she still receives him as kin in a structural sense she does not extend to Norm Webster or, ultimately, to Ronan. Pietro is, irrevocably, Luna's father, and on that axis he retains a permanent low-grade claim on her attention that is operationally relevant even decades after the marriage's end.

---

## SUMMARY MATRIX — FAMILY BONDS, OPERATIONAL

| Figure | Bond Strength | Trust | Leverage on Subject | Direction |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Medusa | Maximal | Absolute | Highest non-Luna | Compliance |
| Luna | Maximal | Absolute | Absolute override | Protection |
| Black Bolt | High | Reverent | Rare-use, high-yield | Compliance |
| Lockjaw | High | Absolute | Protective override | Mutual |
| Gorgon | High | High | Moderate | Fraternal |
| Kar


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

*A mapping of every non-romantic bond of consequence in the subject's life. Romantic and natal-family entries are filed separately. The criterion for inclusion here is sustained relational weight: a person on whom Crystal has, at some documented juncture, either depended for safety, modeled herself after, accepted directives from, extended unusual loyalty toward, or quietly mentored. The list is longer than the casual reader of her file would expect, and the asymmetries between bonds are diagnostically rich.*

---

## 1. Lockjaw

The single most consequential non-human attachment in the subject's life, and the relationship a surveillance file underestimates at its peril.

**History.** Lockjaw has been present in Crystal's environment since before her own Terrigenesis — he predates her self-aware existence. He was the royal family's teleporting companion when she was a small child in Attilan; he was the conveyance that first brought her into Johnny Storm's orbit (*FF* #45 et seq., where Lockjaw carries her on her flight from Maximus); he has been the silent third party in nearly every major geographic relocation of her life, including the transit to the Baxter Building, the returns to the Refuge, the moves to Hala, and the recovery operations of the *Inhuman* and *Royals* eras.

**Dynamics.** Crystal speaks to Lockjaw in a register she uses with no other being in the multiverse. With humans she modulates; with Medusa she defers; with Black Bolt she stills; with Johnny she brightens; with Pietro she braces. With Lockjaw she is *uninflected* — the voice is plain, low, the cadences are the ones she had at twelve. Observable micro-behaviors when alone with him: she sits on the floor rather than in chairs; she rests her hand flat between his shoulder blades while talking (not the head — the spine); she will read or sleep against his flank; she narrates her feelings to him aloud in a way she does to no human, including her own sister.

**Trust / safety.** Maximum. There is no recorded instance of Crystal calculating around Lockjaw, modulating around Lockjaw, or performing for Lockjaw. She does not police her elemental weather in his presence — small breezes and water displacements occur and she does not suppress them. The body relaxes in his vicinity by every legible postural marker: shoulders drop, jaw unclenches, the chronic micro-tension in her hands releases.

**Failure mode.** Lockjaw's loyalty is split across the royal household; in any scenario where his teleportation is required elsewhere, Crystal loses her one source of unwatched solitude with company. She has, in those intervals, decompensated faster than at any other time — the *Silent War* and post-*Infinity* periods both show her affect deteriorating measurably when separated from him. Operationally: removing Lockjaw is removing her single most reliable regulator.

**Leverage.** None usable. Any harm or threat to Lockjaw would produce the same total-mobilization response that threats to Luna produce, and would do so without the ethical brakes that her daughter elicits. He is the only living being who can pull her toward a destination without her requesting it and have her accept the destination unquestioned. This is, in operational terms, the highest-trust relationship in her file.

---

## 2. Karnak Mander-Azur

**History.** Cousin; member of the royal household since her infancy; her childhood instructor in Inhuman philosophy and one of the figures who supervised her preparation for Terrigenesis. Their relationship spans every era of her published life and has cycled through phases: childhood pupil/teacher; young adult mild antagonism (Karnak's austerity vs. her appetite for Earth); mid-career mutual respect (*Inhumans*, Jenkins/Lee); late-career grief partnership (*Royals*).

**Dynamics.** Karnak is the family member who *sees* her dependency pattern most clearly and has, on at least three documented occasions across the canon, named it to her face. The 1998 Jenkins/Lee *Inhumans* run contains a quiet exchange in which Karnak observes that she lives "between" rather than *in* any of her chosen homes, and her response is the only documented instance of her receiving such a diagnosis from a family member without deflection — she did not defend, did not weep, did not change subject. She absorbed it. The absence of recoil is itself the data: Karnak is the one person from whom she will accept hard mirroring.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric. She trusts his judgment absolutely; she does not particularly enjoy his company. The behavioral micro-pattern when Karnak enters a room: she straightens (Medusa-trained reflex) but then *holds his gaze*, where with most family members she looks down or away. The held gaze is the tell — she is allowing herself to be assessed.

**Failure mode.** Karnak's worldview admits no consolation. In moments of high grief — the *Royals*-era losses, Luna's various endangerments — Karnak is the wrong figure to seek and Crystal knows this, and his presence at those moments has produced her sharpest documented snaps at any family member. Twice in canon she has dismissed him with cold formality only to seek him out within a day to apologize. The cycle is stable and they both accept it.

**Leverage.** Karnak is the family member through whom one would route a request requiring Crystal to confront an unwelcome truth. He is the bypass around her Medusa-deference and her Johnny-sentimentality both, because his ask is always framed as *clarity*, never as *duty* or *love*, and clarity is the appeal she has not yet learned to refuse.

---

## 3. Gorgon Petragon

**History.** Cousin, royal guard, longtime household intimate. Childhood relationship was that of the indulgent older relative who let her ride on his shoulders; adolescent relationship shaded into protective gruffness; adult relationship has been one of the most stable in her life precisely because it makes no emotional demand.

**Dynamics.** Gorgon is the family member around whom Crystal eats most freely, jokes most freely, and laughs without monitoring the volume of her laugh. The micro-pattern: she will physically touch Gorgon — a hand on his forearm, a shoulder lean — at frequencies far higher than she touches any other male relative, and the touches are entirely platonic and read by both parties as such. He is the *uncle-coded* figure who lets her be a child again without infantilizing her.

**Trust / safety.** High in the everyday register; not the figure she goes to for existential crisis. He is the figure she goes to for the *first hour* of a crisis — the brute physical reassurance hour — and then routes to Medusa or Karnak for the substance.

**Failure mode.** Gorgon's grief at his own losses (notably the deaths within his own line, recurring across multiple runs) can render him unavailable for weeks at a time, and during those intervals Crystal has historically responded by either (a) escalating her contact with Lockjaw or (b) seeking out a romantic re-engagement. The pattern argues that Gorgon's availability functions as a secondary stabilizer she does not consciously credit.

**Leverage.** Low. Gorgon will not ask anything of her that imposes; correspondingly, requests routed through him register as low-stakes and she may not take them seriously. He is not a vector for serious operational asks.

---

## 4. Triton

**History.** Cousin; presence in her life roughly co-equal to Gorgon in duration, but emotionally cooler. Triton's amphibious physiology and habit of long absences in the deep oceans mean he is one of the family members she has gone longest stretches without seeing.

**Dynamics.** When present, Triton functions as her natural elemental peer — water is the element she handles with greatest intimacy and Triton lives inside it. There is a documented behavioral signature in scenes where both are near the sea: she will mirror his stillness, drop the social performance, and stand at the waterline for extended silent intervals with him. It is the closest thing she has to meditative practice.

**Trust / safety.** Reserved but real. She does not confide in Triton; she *quiets* with him, which for her is a related but distinct form of intimacy.

**Failure mode.** Triton's absences are long and unpredictable. She has learned not to expect him, which means that when he reappears she sometimes over-reacts to the reunion (visible warmth disproportionate to the actual closeness of the bond) and then withdraws again as the reunion ages.

**Leverage.** Triton is the family member who could most credibly invite her to a long sea voyage and have her accept on the strength of the invitation alone. This is operationally niche but worth flagging.

---

## 5. Maximus the Mad

*Separately filed under Adversaries-Family for active threat assessment; included here only for the residual ambivalent-affective component.* The relevant cross-reference: she retains, beneath the entirely justified wariness, a residual fondness for the brother-coded uncle who in her earliest childhood was occasionally kind to her. This residual fondness has been exploited on multiple documented occasions and is the single largest blind spot in her threat-assessment capacity inside the royal household. See the Adversaries file.

---

## 6. Ben Grimm

**History.** Met during her Baxter Building tenure (FF #65 onward); has been a continuous if intermittent presence in her life for the entire subsequent five decades.

**Dynamics.** Ben is the *paternal-coded* friend the file most needs to understand. He treated her, from the outset, as a kid sister rather than as a princess or a girlfriend's appendage, and the categorical clarity of his framing was, for her, profoundly stabilizing. She has never had to perform royalty for Ben; she has never had to perform romance for Ben; she has never had to perform competence for Ben. He sees her as Crystal, full stop, and the absence of role-pressure in the relationship is one of her three or four lifelong emotional anchors.

**Trust / safety.** Very high — perhaps higher than any non-Inhuman human in her file. The behavioral marker is specific: Ben is one of the only humans in whose presence she will eat messily. (For a princess raised in courtly protocol, this is a meaningful unbuttoning.) She also accepts physical correction from him she would not accept from others — a hand on her arm to stop her from a hasty exit, a flat "no, kid" to a half-formed plan — and the corrections land.

**Evolution.** The relationship survived her departure from Johnny, survived the marriage to Pietro, survived the affair, survived everything. Across the Hickman *FF* era and beyond, he is shown to be the Baxter Building figure whose company she most actively seeks when revisiting that space. He does not bring up the past romantic complications. He has never, in all of canon, said an unkind word to her about Johnny or about her own choices.

**Failure mode.** Ben's loyalty to Johnny would, in any scenario where the two are in conflict, prevail. She knows this and does not test it. The relationship is preserved precisely by the unstated agreement not to put it under that load.

**Leverage.** Ben is the single most credible Earth-side vector for getting her to slow down and reconsider a decision. He is also the single most credible vector for getting her to *eat and sleep* during a crisis, which is operationally non-trivial.

---

## 7. Sue Storm-Richards

**History.** Sister of her first love; coterminous presence across the FF tenure and beyond.

**Dynamics.** The relationship has always carried the residue of the Johnny situation — Sue is the older-sister-coded figure who watched Crystal arrive, be loved, leave, and not come back, and whose loyalty to Johnny set a permanent ceiling on the intimacy possible between them. Within that ceiling, the bond is real. Sue extended genuine maternal attention to Crystal during her adolescent FF tenure (cooking, clothing logistics, the small practical care that Crystal had never received from a peer-mother figure), and Crystal absorbed it with measurable gratitude.

**Trust / safety.** Medium-high in the everyday register; constrained on the topic of Johnny, where Sue's loyalty is total and Crystal knows it. The behavioral signature: Crystal will discuss virtually anything with Sue *except* her current feelings about Johnny, and will redirect the conversation with notable smoothness whenever it drifts there.

**Evolution.** As both women aged into motherhood, a parallel-mother bond emerged — Luna and Franklin/Valeria as the connective tissue. The exchange of parenting notes has been one of the more stable and gendered intimacies of her adult life.

**Failure mode.** Sue's primary loyalty is to her own household. In any conflict between Crystal's needs and the Richards/Storm family's needs, Crystal will be the one to accommodate, and both women know it without saying so.

**Leverage.** Sue is the figure whose disapproval Crystal most fears among non-Inhumans. A clear statement from Sue that a course of action would be unwise is one of the few interventions that consistently alters her behavior.

---

## 8. Reed Richards

**History.** Father-figure adjacent during her FF tenure; intermittent collaborator thereafter (notably the *Infinity* and Illuminati-adjacent arcs).

**Dynamics.** Reed is one of the very few figures in her life who has consistently treated her as a *technical mind* rather than a princess, a girlfriend, or a daughter. He has, in multiple documented exchanges, asked her substantive questions about Inhuman science and Terrigen biology and *listened to her answers*. This is rarer in her experience than the file's casual reader will appreciate. She has noticeably elevated her own register in his presence — speaks in longer sentences, allows herself technical vocabulary, drops the diplomatic warmth in favor of a precision she does not display elsewhere.

**Trust / safety.** Cognitively high; emotionally moderate. He is not a confidant. He is a respected adult whose respect she values.

**Failure mode.** Reed's preoccupation with his own work has left her in lurches at moments she could have used his attention. She does not hold this against him; she expects it. She has organized her expectations around his unavailability rather than challenging it.

**Leverage.** Reed is the figure whose framing of a problem in *systems* terms she will accept where she would resist the same framing from a family member. A scientific framing of a personal crisis routes around her defenses.

---

## 9. Medusa — *cross-reference, primary natal-family file*

Filed in full under Natal Family. The relevant cross-cutting note for this section: Medusa is *simultaneously* the most consequential mentor relationship in Crystal's life and the most consequential dependency vector, and the entanglement of those two roles is the single most persistent structural problem in the subject's psychology. Every other mentor relationship in this section is in part an attempt to obtain a piece of what Medusa provides without the cost Medusa extracts.

---

## 10. Black Bolt — *cross-reference, primary natal-family file*

Filed in full under Natal Family. The relevant cross-cutting note: Crystal experiences Black Bolt as a *climate* rather than a person — his silent gravitas is something she lives inside rather than transacts with. He is paternal-coded but the paternity is impersonal. She has never received from him the focused, individuated attention that a daughter-figure typically requires, and she has internalized the absence as natural. This means she does not look for paternal-coded attention from other male figures, which is one of the things that has kept her romantic life from being even more chaotic than it has been.

---

## 11. Quake (Daisy Johnson)

**History.** Late-career relationship, primarily *Inhuman* (2014–15) and adjacent. Daisy entered Crystal's orbit as a peer-leader during the NuHuman crisis, technically Inhuman by descent but cultured outside Attilan entirely.

**Dynamics.** This is the relationship in which Crystal most clearly occupies the *senior* position, and the data is revealing — she handles seniority with grace, neither over-mothering nor under-supporting, providing the kind of structured guidance she herself never received from a peer mentor. The behavioral signature: Crystal in Daisy's presence is markedly more decisive than Crystal in any other peer context. Mentoring activates her competent self.

**Trust / safety.** Medium and rising. Both women are guarded by training; both recognize the guard in the other; both respect it.

**Failure mode.** Daisy's institutional loyalties (SHIELD-coded) cut against Inhuman interests at multiple junctures, and Crystal has had to navigate those frictions without rupturing the relationship. She has done so successfully but at the cost of never fully relaxing into the bond.

**Leverage.** Operationally, Daisy is the figure most likely to bring Crystal credible threat-intelligence from human institutional sources, and Crystal will weight that intelligence heavily.

---

## 12. Ms. Marvel (Kamala Khan)

**History.** Late-career; the NuHuman generation; Kamala registers in Crystal's file as the *protégée-coded* young woman to whom she has extended the warmest mentoring of her life.

**Dynamics.** Crystal recognized in Kamala, almost immediately, the version of herself she might have been with better scaffolding — Inhuman-by-descent, raised inside a loving non-Inhuman family, possessed of an unselfconscious moral clarity Crystal acquired only late and partially. She has been measured in her contact with Kamala — careful not to import Kamala into the Inhuman court's dysfunctions, careful not to project — and the restraint is itself the mentoring.

**Trust / safety.** High and protective. Crystal extends to Kamala the protection she extends to Luna.

**Failure mode.** Crystal's protectiveness can shade into over-shielding, withholding from Kamala information Kamala has a right to. She has caught herself doing this at least once in canon and corrected.

**Leverage.** None usable without crossing the protection cordon, which would terminate the operator's standing with the subject permanently.

---

## 13. Iso (Xiaoyi Chen)

**History.** *Inhuman*-era recruit, NuHuman, Crystal's direct trainee.

**Dynamics.** The protégée relationship in which Crystal most fully inhabited the role she would have wanted from Medusa — present, patient, individuating rather than directive. Iso received from Crystal the *unconditional positive regard plus structured challenge* that Crystal herself had never received in the same combination.

**Trust / safety.** High, paternalistic-tilting; Crystal monitors this and works against the tilt.

**Failure mode.** Crystal's investment in Iso's development is partly displaced investment in her own arrested development, and this can produce overreach in moments where Iso needs space rather than guidance.

**Leverage.** Iso is the figure whose disappointment in Crystal would land most painfully, because it would be the disappointment of a self-projection.

---

## 14. Flint, Naja, Grid, and the broader NuHuman cohort

Filed collectively. Crystal's relationship to the NuHuman generation as a whole is that of an *elder sister of the diaspora* — she has taken seriously the burden of welcoming people into an Inhuman identity they did not choose. The work has stabilized her. It is the only sustained context in which she has functioned in the *giving* rather than *receiving* end of a care relationship across an extended interval, and the effect on her self-concept has been notably positive.

---

## 15. The Avengers (cohort)

**History.** Active member across the Stern/Englehart era and intermittently thereafter (West Coast tenure, *Royals*-adjacent crossovers).

**Dynamics.** She has never been an *Avengers central* figure in the way she has been an Inhumans central figure; she has been a *contributing member* whose loyalty is real but whose primary identification lies elsewhere. The cohort treats her with affection and respect; she returns same; the bond is institutional rather than intimate.

**Notable individual within the cohort: the Vision.** During her West Coast Avengers tenure, the Vision and Wanda were extended-family-by-marriage (Pietro's twin sister and her synthezoid spouse), and Crystal interacted with the Vision in a register of measured ease. He was, for her, a figure whose emotional steadiness she found restorative during the Pietro-collapse period. There is no romantic dimension; the relationship was a quietly stabilizing friendship.

**Notable individual within the cohort: Hawkeye (Clint Barton).** West Coast tenure brought sustained contact. The behavioral signature was *peer ease* — she relaxed around his irreverence in ways she rarely did around the more formal Avengers. He did not flirt with her and she did not flirt with him; the relationship was clean and warm.

**Failure mode.** Her divided loyalty (Inhumans first) has at moments produced friction with Avengers operational requirements. She has navigated this honestly but at cost.

**Leverage.** Operationally moderate; institutional channels yield institutional cooperation.

---

## 16. Wanda Maximoff

**History.** Sister-in-law for the duration of the Pietro marriage; sister-in-law-emerita thereafter; one of the longest-running female relationships in her file.

**Dynamics.** This is the most psychologically complicated friendship in Crystal's life and the file should not soften the complication. The two women love each other genuinely. The two women have also navigated, between them, every conceivable load — Pietro's instability, Wanda's own catastrophic breakdowns, the affair and its aftermath, the custody negotiations over Luna, Wanda's reality-warping episodes, the periods of mutual blame and mutual reconciliation. The relationship has survived because both women have, at critical junctures, chosen survival of the bond over scoring of the point.

The behavioral signature when they meet after long absence: a long held embrace, often silent; one of the very few intimacies in Crystal's life that does not require speech to function.

**Trust / safety.** High in the emotional register; constrained in the Pietro register, where both women carry information about him the other does not want to hear.

**Failure mode.** Wanda's reality-warping has, at moments, put Crystal and Luna at risk through no malice of Wanda's own, and Crystal has had to hold the awareness of that risk alongside the love. She has done so without rupture but the cognitive load is real.

**Leverage.** None advisable. The bond is one of the structural supports of her adult life and any attempt to weaponize it would be detected and would terminate the operator's standing across both women's networks simultaneously.

---

## 17. Ronan the Accuser — *cross-reference, primary romantic-history file*

Filed in full under Romantic. Cross-cutting note: post-dissolution, the residual relationship has functions of an *alliance* rather than a marriage, and Ronan has on at least one documented occasion functioned as a strategic resource she could call on. The bond Earth-side observers underestimate.

---

## 18. Locus, the Royal Household Staff, and the Old Servants of Attilan

A surveillance file is incomplete without the household staff. Crystal was raised by a rotating constellation of caretakers, tutors, and attendants whose names rarely surface in published canon but whose collective presence shaped her capacity for ease with service personnel. She knows the names of the staff of every household she has lived in. She greets them by name. She does not summon; she requests. She does not interrupt their meals. This is, in part, courtly training; it is also genuine. Operationally: any infiltration vector through household staff is closed by the simple fact that the staff *like her*, in a way they do not like every member of the royal household, and would warn her.

---

## 19


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

A dossier on Crystalia Amaquelin that omits the romantic and adversarial axis omits the load-bearing wall of the architecture. Her enemies have been comparatively few and her lovers comparatively numerous, and several figures occupy both columns at different points in the longitudinal record. What follows is the granular file on each.

---

## I. LOVERS & INTIMATES

### Jonathan Lowell Spencer "Johnny" Storm — The First Imprint

**History.** First encounter: *Fantastic Four* #45, 1965, in the Hidden Land. She is hiding in an alcove of Attilan during Maximus's siege; he finds her, she touches his face, and the imprint takes inside a single page. She is, in canonical terms, an adolescent at the moment of meeting; he is not much older. They reunite across the mid-arc and by *FF* #65–81 she has effectively eloped from the Inhuman court to live in the Baxter Building. The cohabitation runs roughly four publishing years and ends in *FF* #105 when the pollution allergy forces her evacuation. Pietro arrives at the rescue threshold within issues.

The relationship has been resurrected three times since: a flirtation rekindling during the late-80s Englehart *FF*, the Hickman/Robinson re-engagement during the 2010–14 Future Foundation arcs, and a quieter adult resonance throughout *Inhuman* and *Royals*.

**Dynamics.** The defining feature is *first-ness*. Johnny is the only partner Crystal chose without dynastic pressure, geographic compulsion, or rebound velocity behind her — and the choice was made by a teenager fleeing a coup. The relationship therefore carries a permanent over-valuation in her file: every subsequent partner is, on some level, evaluated against an idealized adolescent benchmark that the actual Johnny Storm has never been able to match in adulthood, because the adult Johnny is a more limited, more restless figure than the rescuer she met at fourteen.

Behaviorally with him she is at her most performatively *normal*: she dresses down, attempts ordinary New York routines, learns ice cream and movies and traffic. She is also at her most somatically distressed — the pollution episode is real, and so is the chronic low-grade homesickness that pre-dates it.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust is total but is held at the level of *imprint*, not negotiation. She has never had to test whether Johnny would betray her because she has never put him in a position where betrayal would cost him anything. Conversely, she has betrayed him by absence — leaving without fight, taking his ring off in *FF* #150, marrying his rival within weeks. He has metabolized this as her being "the one that got away" rather than as injury.

**Failure Mode.** The somatic exit. When the bond becomes effortful she will not negotiate; she will leave on medical or familial pretext, accept the verdict, and reattach. Any reactivation of this pair has a known half-life.

**Leverage.** Sustained — forty real-world years on, his presence in any room measurably alters her decision tempo (she defers more, looks at him before answering). Any actor wishing to slow her, redirect her, or pull her toward sentimentality routes through Johnny. Conversely, any actor wishing to *anger* Pietro presents Crystal-and-Johnny tableaux, which historically works.

---

### Pietro Maximoff — The Long Catastrophe

**History.** Introduced as her caretaker post-pollution in *FF* #150 (1974); married in the same issue under what reads, even by Bronze Age compression standards, as accelerated circumstances. Luna Maximoff born approximately *Avengers* #200 era. Marriage progressively destabilizes across his *Avengers* run, his entanglement with the High Evolutionary, and the revelations around Bova and his parentage. The Norm Webster affair surfaces in *West Coast Avengers* (1985–86 vicinity). Public collapse, custody dispute, multiple reconciliations through the late Lobdell and Abnett/Lanning eras, the *Son of M* and *Silent War* fallout, the further breaks across *Avengers: The Children's Crusade* and beyond. They have, depending on how one counts, separated and reconciled at least five times.

**Dynamics.** This is the relationship in which her dependent traits and his control traits found, catastrophically, a mutually reinforcing key-and-lock. Pietro requires a partner who will not challenge his velocity; Crystal requires a partner who will plot her trajectory for her. The fit was real and it was poison. His paternal-coded interventions (managing her recovery, choosing where they live, dictating Luna's upbringing) replicated the Black Bolt/Medusa authority structure she had supposedly left — which is precisely what made it homelike.

The escalating asymmetry: his speed both literal and cognitive runs ahead of her affective processing, so disagreements end before she can form a position. Over years this produced a learned helplessness specific to him — observable in panel: shoulders drop, voice softens, sentences shorten in his presence in ways they do not around anyone else.

**Trust / Safety.** Functionally zero by the late 1980s, although the formal trust ritual continues. She does not believe he will be present, will keep his word about Luna, or will refrain from sudden ideological reversals. He does not believe she will not flee. Both are correct.

**Failure Mode.** The affair. Confronted with his neglect she did not confront him; she went sideways into Norm. This is the defining behavioral exhibit of her file and Pietro is the partner against whom it was performed. Any subsequent partner who reproduces Pietro's pattern of velocity-plus-absence should expect the same response within eighteen months.

**Leverage.** Luna. He is the co-parent and any operation against Crystal that *threatens Luna via Pietro* (or vice versa) collapses both their tactical postures simultaneously. Secondary leverage: his instability is publicly known to her; presenting evidence of a fresh Pietro breakdown will pull her toward intervention even after decades of estrangement.

---

### Norm Webster — The Pressure Valve

**History.** A Los Angeles realtor she meets while attached to the West Coast Avengers; the affair runs concurrent with the disintegrating Pietro marriage, surfaces, becomes public knowledge, and is the proximate trigger for the formal separation. He is ordinary in every dimension that matters: no powers, no politics, no surname that maps to a dynasty, a job that involves house keys and signatures.

**Dynamics.** This is the most diagnostically transparent relationship in her file precisely because *Norm himself is almost incidental*. He is the type-specimen of what she reaches for under anxious-preoccupied collapse: a calm, available, low-stakes human male whose ordinariness functions as anti-Pietro. The relationship does not survive the disclosure because it was never structured to; it was a parallel attachment doing reality-testing work, not a candidate primary bond.

**Trust / Safety.** High while it lasted, in the specific sense that he had no agenda and no capacity to harm her politically. Low in the structural sense that she was using him and on some level both parties knew it.

**Failure Mode.** Exposure. The affair pattern only works in concealment; once aired it becomes a stick the family system uses to discipline her, and she does not have the confrontational machinery to defend the choice in public.

**Leverage.** Historical, not active. Norm is no longer a live figure in her orbit, but the *category* of Norm — the safe ordinary man at the moment of bond crisis — is a permanent vulnerability in her file. Any future Pietro-equivalent partner should expect a Norm-equivalent to surface during the second year of strain.

---

### Ronan the Accuser — The Arrangement That Became Real

**History.** Dynastically betrothed during the Kree-Inhuman alignment of *Silent War* / *War of Kings* (2007–2009, Hine and the Abnett/Lanning cosmic arc). She accepts. The marriage is consummated as state instrument; she relocates to Hala; over months it becomes — by her own internal narration — a real bond, on which Ronan's eventual fate inflicts genuine grief.

**Dynamics.** The clinically interesting relationship of her adult life. Presented with a partner she did not choose, in a marriage structured as political instrument, she did not refuse, did not sabotage, and did not maintain inner reservation. She *metabolized the arrangement into felt love*. This is rare and it tells us something the other relationships obscure: she has a capacity to generate attachment within almost any structure, which means her bonds are at least partly a function of *the structure of the bond itself* rather than the specific other party. Ronan was austere, hierarchical, formal, and assigned — and the assignment-quality was, paradoxically, restful for her after the Pietro chaos.

**Trust / Safety.** Higher than the Pietro marriage at its equivalent stage. Ronan's rigidity, often diagnosed by other parties as a weakness, was for Crystal a *predictability*, which read as safety. He did not lie to her, did not vanish, did not contradict himself between Tuesday and Friday.

**Failure Mode.** External — his death/political collapse, not internal rupture. Notably this is the only major relationship of her life she did not exit through her own behavioral pattern; it was ended *for* her, which is part of why the grief was so unguarded.

**Leverage.** Post-Ronan she has developed, for the first time in her file, an explicit allergic response to *being framed as a political instrument*. Anyone repeating that framing, even in the service of genuine Inhuman interest, will now meet sharper resistance than at any prior point in her life. This is the one bright-line shift the Ronan marriage permanently installed.

---

### Lineage, Flirtations, and Secondary Intimacies

**Quicksilver-Crystal era flings adjacent to Avengers tenure.** Across her Avengers and West Coast Avengers years there are repeated low-grade attachments and near-flirtations (a stretch of warmth with Hercules; a quieter dynamic with the Vision during the Pietro-Wanda overlap). None of these consummate; each fits the pattern of testing whether the bond-machinery still works while remaining inside the marriage envelope.

**Black Bolt — non-romantic but worth noting in this section.** The brother-in-law relationship is the closest she has to a paternal attachment. His silence functions for her the way an analyst's silence functions for a patient: she has projected onto him, for fifty years, a steady benevolent attention that may or may not be wholly there. She trusts him absolutely on Inhuman matters and would accept an instruction from him she would refuse from any other figure. The detonation of Attilan in *Infinity* did not break this trust — she absorbed it as duty.

**Triton, Karnak, Gorgon — cousins, never lovers; permanent extended family.** Filed under "family" but worth flagging here because Crystal's romantic radius has never extended *within* the royal house, which is itself a data point: she exogamizes consistently, every romantic figure has been outside Attilan. The princess who only loves foreigners.

---

## II. RIVALS

### Medusalith Amaquelin Boltagon — Sister, Sovereign, Rival

The rivalry register with Medusa is real but largely sublimated. Crystal has, across sixty years, accepted Medusa's directives with surface poise while engaging in low-grade passive resistance: late arrivals, half-finished diplomatic remits, the Norm affair (which was a betrayal of *Pietro* and through him of Medusa's brokered alliances), the *Royals* departure (which was geographic exit framed as duty). Trust is high, rivalry is unspoken, leverage is enormous in either direction. Medusa is the only figure who can route an instruction past Crystal's late-career assertiveness by invoking sisterhood. Conversely, Crystal is the only figure who can wound Medusa via Luna or via reminder of Crystal's own pre-queen freedoms. (Fuller dynamic in the Family section; flagged here because Medusa is the *permanent silent rival* in every romantic and political theater of Crystal's life.)

### Quicksilver — Rival as Ex-Husband

Pietro now occupies the rare double position of former primary attachment and active adversary across multiple custody and ideological flashpoints. The rivalry is intimate, asymmetric, and continuous: he competes for Luna, for moral standing within the extended Maximoff/Inhuman/Avenger ecology, and for the historical narrative of who failed whom. She does not engage publicly. She wins quietly, repeatedly, by simply being more stable than he is. Leverage flows in both directions and neither will use it to full effect because of Luna.

### Maximus the Mad — Inherited Enemy

Crystal's animus toward Maximus is family-coded rather than personal. He is the one who drove her into hiding in *FF* #45 and therefore, in a strict causal sense, the figure responsible for the Johnny Storm meeting — a fact she has likely never consciously formulated. She fights him competently when required, mistrusts him absolutely, and does not engage him in the ambivalent register her siblings use. He cannot bargain with her. He has, on occasion, attempted manipulation via promises about Luna; this is a clean failure mode for him because Luna-threat consolidates her opposition rather than splits it.

### Ahura — Complicated Adjacency

Black Bolt and Medusa's son is not a rival in any straightforward sense, but the *Royals*-era and adjacent material puts Crystal in repeated friction with him over command authority on the Astarith and over Inhuman succession matters. She handles him as an aunt handles a difficult nephew who outranks her: deference layered over correction. He cannot be trusted to be stable; she can be trusted to absorb his instability without retaliation. Low rivalry, high containment cost.

### Ronan (post-betrothal political residue) — Kree Court Factions

She inherited, with the marriage, a set of Kree court enemies who viewed the Inhuman alliance as dilution. These figures persist as latent adversaries even after Ronan's death; she retains some standing in Kree protocol and would be recognized in a Hala throne room, which is itself a vulnerability — anyone seeking to lure her offworld can do so via a Kree protocol pretext that her sense of duty will not refuse.

---

## III. ENEMIES — Standing Adversaries

### The Unspoken — Black Bolt's Reading List of Threats She Inherited

By virtue of marriage, sisterhood, Avengers tenure, FF tenure, and Kree alliance, Crystal has inherited the enemy lists of five distinct power structures. The relevant ones for her active file:

- **The Kree Supreme Intelligence and its court factions** — perceives her as both asset and dilution; treats her in formal protocol; would deploy against her via political framing rather than direct attack.
- **Skrull remnants from *Secret Invasion*** — she was identified and infiltrated-adjacent during the Veranke years; residual operational interest exists. She is appropriately paranoid about identity verification of intimates after this episode, a habit observable in subtle re-checks during reunions.
- **The High Evolutionary** — via Pietro and Wanda's genetic history, by extension via Luna's lineage. He has at multiple points evinced interest in Luna's genome. This is the single highest-priority external threat in her file because it routes through her one absolute pressure point.
- **Anti-Inhuman mutant factions during the Terrigen Cloud crisis (*Death of X*, *IvX*)** — most consequentially Emma Frost's faction during and after the Cyclops martyrdom. Crystal was not the primary target but was a visible representative of the Inhuman position; residual animus exists in those quarters.
- **Anti-mutant factions reciprocally** — symmetric residue.
- **Vulcan / Shi'ar Imperial residue from *War of Kings*** — old enmity, dormant but real.

### Maximus — see Rivals; functionally an enemy too.

### Thanos / Black Order — *Infinity* era
